--- 帖子 #1 ---
Dear all,

Here I present to you my new System, AshFX Daily. It's excellent for traders who work a full-time job, and/or can't/don't want to spend hours and hours staring at the screen.

I’ve been working on this system for quite a while; I wanted to make it accurate, yet simple at the same time.  I believe I have achieved that.  It is designed for the Daily Timeframe, and can be used on any currency pair.

The results that can be obtained from this system, is literally hundreds of pips a month. On average, the reward is greater than the risk.

These are the indicators that are required:

-   Parabolic Stop and Reverse (PSAR, 0.03, 0.2)

-   AC (Accelerator Oscillator)

-   AO (Awesome Oscillator)

-   Stochastics (5,3,3)

Take the attached template and apply it in Metatrader. Use it on the Daily Timeframe (D1), on any currency pair. By the way, these indicators can be found in any platform, so you are not limited to MT4.

See below for an example of what you should be seeing:

Two files attached - the actual AshFX System PDF manual, and the template for MT4 users. Please read carefully.

Look forward to questions/analysis/discussion/testing.

Regards,

Ash

--- 帖子 #100 ---
To Ronald:

I haven't read your code yet but am wondering this as I don't see it reflected in your features list:

About the SAR characteristics (for a "first strength" trade entry):

We're supposed to enter after the close of the first candle (= on the open of the second candle) on which the PSAR has changed places. That would mean the previous PSAR is on the same side, and the second previous is on the other side.

So the conditions on the list would be (let's say on Day1, Day2, Day3):

for LONG entries:

PSAR below price (Day 3) > PSAR previous candle (Day 2) < PSAR Day 1 (which would be above price).

for SHORT entries:

PSAR above price (Day 3) < PSAR previous candle (Day 2) > PSAR Day 1 (which would be below price).

If it's already taken account of, please disregard this message

--- 帖子 #102 ---
It's there don't worry. It's through the EachTickMode feature.

If set to true, the EA will take a signal as soon as it sees one.

If set to false, the EA will take a signal at the end of the bar.

Some people think it's better to enter when you see the signal, and others think it's better to enter at the close of a bar.

--- 帖子 #118 ---
Looks like you're in the complete trading system. AshFX as opposed to AshFX Entry Only.

The code ifgnores Takeprofit and Stoploss, and replaces those with the high/low where appropriate.

The trailing stop function will override the existing SL. If the SL due to trailing stop is tighter than the current SL, the SL will be changed. Otherwise, those settings look good.

--- 帖子 #120 ---
Nvwine - correct, the swing low is exactly that, 0.9818. So yep, if you look at the trade, it was a "Second Strength Trade", because the Stochs has crossed the 50 line, which is why the initial SL would be placed at 0.9818, making the SL = 119 pips to be precise.

So, like I mentioned in the PDF, we always enter two positions of equal size lots. We enter at the start of the next day at 0.9936. The first TP would be equal to the previous candle's close minus it's low, which is 0.9937 - 0.9867 = 70.  I.e. our first TP on our first position would be 70 pips. As soon as this is hit, we move our SL on our second position to break even, i.e. new SL is @ 0.9936.

We let the remaning second position ride until the AO closes as a red colour, which happened tonight, thus price closing @ 1.0184. Which meant our second position made us 248 pips.

So in total, for that USD/CAD trade you're looking at 248 + 70 = 318 pips.  Hope this makes sense.

(Apologies for my 1000 pip outburst, I had entered multiple positions and got excited, ahem. Been working on different MM strategies for this system but haven't mentioned that as of yet.)

--- 帖子 #138 ---
Thanks Tonny.

PSAR does not repaint. Obviously the signal will adjust DURING candle formation, but once the candle has closed, it stays put.

And since we only enter on the close of a candle (i.e. start of a new candle), then for our purposes it's perfect.

--- 帖子 #143 ---
It's in the "final points" of the method:

"Please bear in mind that when entering a trade, it doesn't matter in which order the indicators may line up, e.g. the AO and AC don't have to change colour at the same candle as the first PSAR dot appearing. Or perhaps the AO / AC / Stochs might be compliant before the first PSAR dot appears, or vice versa, and this is fine."

--- 帖子 #146 ---
Entry is only made on the appearance of the PSAR.

--- 帖子 #147 ---
What this means is, it doesn't matter which order the AO or AC or Stochs line up...  So either AO can come before AC, or vice versa, or AC can come before Stochs or vice versa, or AO can come before Stochs or vice versa.  It doesn't matter. But as long as they all line up when the PSAR appears it's cool. I.e. they don't all have to change on the same candle.

What DOES matter is that we only take trades upon the close of the first PSAR dot.

Hope this clarifies things, and apologies for the ambuigity.

--- 帖子 #148 ---
Hi, the candle HAS to be compliant when the first PSAR dot appears.

((EachTickMode && !TickCheck) || (!EachTickMode && (Bars != BarCount)))

--- 帖子 #213 ---
Exactly dude.  I prefer price action to determine my SL and TP. Using fixed stops and tp's are way too rigid. Not saying they don't work, but price action rules. Maybe some systems suit fixed SL/TP, (e.g. scalping systems), but mine definitely doesn't.

--- 帖子 #214 ---
It means that if the PSAR is below the candle, then the candle must be green. If the PSAR is above the candle, then the candle needs to be red.

You only enter when you see the first PSAR dot. You can't enter after 3/4 dots have appeared.

S/R levels are something that can't be explained in 1 post. You need to practice, and train your eye. There are many threads on Forexfactory dedicated to Support and Resistance.

--- 帖子 #272 ---
Whatever happens on Sunday or Monday is not going to change the Friday candle in anyway.

The price could move for you or against you between Friday and Monday and will only affect your entry point but your stop would not change so I would be inclined to say place your order immediately after the Friday close.

--- 帖子 #281 ---
Hi all,

As Ash said we dont have to risk more than 3% on a trade. What does it exactly mean? Imagine I opened an account with USD 500. Give me an example please!

--- 帖子 #282 ---
www.babypips.com will have ur answer!!

sonic

--- 帖子 #283 ---
3% of $500 is $15.

$15 is what you can risk = stop loss on that trade.

You will need a micro account (positions from 0,01 lots = 1 pip equals $0,10), as with a mini account you would only be able to place a 15 pips stop loss.

On a micro account: $15 on a 0,01 lot is 150 pips (150 x $0,10 = $15)

If you only need a 50 pips stop loss, you would be able to open a 0,03 lot position (50 x $0,30 = $15).

And so on.

--- 帖子 #307 ---
You have a Sunday bar and FXDD does not. That means you have 6 days in your trading week. This changes the calculations of the indicators. Less important but worth noting, IBFX's new day starts 3 hours later.

If you want to learn this system right use FXDD. That is what Ash, the system's creator uses. You can always run both the FXDD and IBFX platforms. Another platform with some adjustments may work as well or better than FXDD. It is hard to tell at this point. But learn the system first then you can compare platforms and try to optimize the settings you use.

--- 帖子 #341 ---
Thanks ASH for the encouragement. I'm learning on these long time frames you have to hold em and have a stomach for negative pippage in order to let these trades play out. Even if you hit your stop loss you have to follow the rules and look for the next setup. Unlike Pipnailer on the lower TF's these are long term and more productive. So you end up trading less, with higher probability and profitability. It is a mindset that has to be developed through repetitive practice and taking losses is all part of it. The beauty of this beast is more time away from the computer and not having to look at charts on lower tf's constantly going back anf forth to confirm indicators.

--- 帖子 #342 ---
I think you need the [1] with Open and Close to check the prior day instead of the newly formed bar. Hardly any trades passed the Stoch test from an EA point of view when used as a daily trader. (This may be because the EA is checking the Stoch on the newly formed bar? haven't figured it out yet)  I used the numbers below to start with before changing to variables on my daily trader.

I changed that part of the code to
Inserted Code if(AC1 > AC2 && AO1 > AO2 && PSAR < Middle && Open[1] < Close[1] && StochMain < 80 && StochSignal < 65 && StochMain > StochMain1 && StochSignal > StochSignal1 && StochMain > StochSignal) Order = SIGNAL_BUY;
if(AC1 < AC2 && AO1 < AO2 && PSAR > Middle && Open[1] > Close[1] && StochMain > 20 && StochSignal > 35 && StochMain < StochMain1 && StochSignal < StochSignal1 && StochMain < StochSignal) Order = SIGNAL_SELL;
With 'Every Tick' set to false I could never get a true condition out of either side of the || using the following code:
Inserted Code if (Order == SIGNAL_SELL && ((EachTickMode && !TickCheck) || (!EachTickMode && (Bars != BarCount))))
I don't know how to program well enough to know why it does not work so I cut out most of it for daily trading and used something like the following to make a daily only trader.
Inserted Code
if (Hour() == 0 && (Minute() <= 15))
{
TradeNow = True;
}
else
{
TradeNow = false;
}

if ((Order == SIGNAL_BUY ) && (TradeNow == true))
I also changed
Inserted Code          Ticket1 = OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask, Slippage, Low[0], Ask + (Ask - Low[0]), "Buy(#" + MagicNumber + ") Trade #1", MagicNumber, 0, DodgerBlue);
Ticket2 = OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask, Slippage, Low[0], Ask + (Ask - Low[0]), "Buy(#" + MagicNumber + ") Trade #2", MagicNumber, 0, DodgerBlue);
To
Inserted Code          Ticket1 = OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask, Slippage, Low[1], Ask + (Ask - Low[1]), "Buy(#" + MagicNumber + ") Trade #1", MagicNumber, 0, DodgerBlue);
Ticket2 = OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask, Slippage, Low[1], Ask + (Ask - Low[1]), "Buy(#" + MagicNumber + ") Trade #2", MagicNumber, 0, DodgerBlue);
If the Stoch test is too low, a new test needs to be added to avoid re-entry on a trade recently closed at TP. I used a PSAR test checking to see if middle had changed in the last 3 bars.

On the AskFX EA I am playing with having the second trade's SL being moved to BE+?? when the first trade closes for a profit. Then trailing the second trade by a large amount. Making sure the EA does not open any more trades while the one trade is still open.

--- 帖子 #361 ---
I'll be showing my newb-ness here for sure, but I haven't used the PSAR in depth at all.

I just noticed something interesting, though... when the dot changes sides, its value is the same as the most recent corresponding swing high or low.

So in other words, the value of the USDJPY dot on 6/20 is 108.57, which is the same swing high value of the candle on 6/16 from which it is calculated.

Most of you probably already know this, but it will help me figure out where to place my stops for secondary trades in the future.

-Dave

--- 帖子 #367 ---
I do not want to post any EAs in this thread. Ron makes corrections properly. I make dirty 'cut and paste', 'work around', type of edits. I feel it is problematic long term to have a bunch of poorly modified EAs spread through a thread. I don't want to turn Ash's thread into a discussion of which EA is better and which version is correct. I am doing more back testing. If I find additional areas that I think Ron may want to look at I will post it.

As I said in a previous post the EA trades as written just very seldom. This does not mean the EA is not working properly. The EA is mechanical. It does not use common sense. These EAs are not designed to enter SS Trades. I have attached a chart for the GBPUSD. I'm sure if you traded manually you would find more than 2 entries in 3 months. I checked all of them and the EA with default settings was trading properly in my opinion.

Any results posted from the EAs should not be considered when evaluating Ash's system. It is not easy to get an expert to trade the same as a skilled eye following all the rules.

I don't know if changing the Stoch values is the proper way to increase EA trades. I mentioned what I did before for debugging purposes.

If you do want to play with the EA, the two lines where I modified the Stoch values for my back test were next to each other in the Signal Begin(Entry) section of the EA. You could try some numbers like I did below. If you enter too many bad trades you will have to move closer to the defaults.
Inserted Code if(AC1 > AC2 && AO1 > AO2 && PSAR < Middle && iOpen(NULL, 0, Current + 0) < iClose(NULL, 0, Current + 0) && [b]StochMain < 80 && StochSignal < 70[/b] && StochMain > StochMain1 && StochSignal > StochSignal1 && StochMain > StochSignal) Order = SIGNAL_BUY;
if(AC1 < AC2 && AO1 < AO2 && PSAR > Middle && iOpen(NULL, 0, Current + 0) > iClose(NULL, 0, Current + 0) && [b]StochMain > 20 && StochSignal > 30[/b] && StochMain < StochMain1 && StochSignal < StochSignal1 && StochMain < StochSignal) Order = SIGNAL_SELL;

--- 帖子 #369 ---
I've changed the EAs so the Stoch level requirements are variable.

StochUpper is the limit the Stoch main and signal must be below in order to be a BUY

StochLower is the limit the Stoch main and signal must be above in order to be a SELL

--- 帖子 #371 ---
If there's anything I've learned about Ash's systems is that they generally take a lot of time between signals on a single pair, and there's good reason for that.

Mechanical trading revolves around one main concept: The market has repeated-predictable imperfections where we can determine which way it needs to go.

So, yes, I guess it's okay to relax the rules just to make sure the EA takes the trades, but once that's established, return the settings to the system spec.

--- 帖子 #376 ---
Hi Ror,

Yes, I entered my SS Long Trade for Eur/Jpy at the opening of the new candle, i.e. 165.18.  My SL was at the swing low, which was @ 161.73.

My 1st TP (as outlined in the PDF manual in the first post), is equal to the same number of pips of the close of the candle minus the low, which is 165.17 - 162.24 = 293 pips.  This TP was hit, and I moved my SL to break even.

The second TP was when the AO closed as red. This occured yesterday, at which point I closed my long for an additional 215 pips.

So in total, on that trade I made around 500 pips.

Hope the pic makes things clearer.

Ash is right.  The problem I'm seeing is that many of you are using real live accounts to test the system.  That's taking on more risk than necessary.  You should be testing with a demo account unless you hate money.

--- 帖子 #391 ---
Personally, I don't recommend trading for too long on demo accounts. In my opinion, to test a system, it's better to open a live micro account (tenth of a mini), and then test. This way, you're working with real money, and it will instill in to you the required attributes you need to cope with natural human emotions such as greed, fear, hope, etc...

--- 帖子 #392 ---
also, systems are often a product of the specific market they were developed in. waiting too long to impliment a system could see the market conditions change and the system losing its effectiveness.

of course the best systems overcome that, which is the hope for every system developer.

--- 帖子 #397 ---
Then that would be a system in which I am not interested. I would even go as far as question how good that system is.  Nobody can predict when the market conditions will change. If you try to do that you will have lost your shirt. That's not a good approach to trading.

--- 帖子 #398 ---
That's fine for you. The point of testing a system is to see whether it works or not. I've tested too many systems that don't work to put blind faith into something to which I'm just introduced. Moreover, I see so many people on here repeatedly ask the same questions about the rules of the system. Why would I use my hard earned money to test something especially if I'm not sure of the rules? That makes no sense. They also want to bail on trades when things start looking down. You are not going to effectively test a system if you have the fear of losing money because of a system in which you haven't built trust. You're not going to know if the system is any good if you keep bailing on trades because you have this fear of losing money. The better approach to me is to first test on a demo, then once you're familiar and comfortable with the system go live, even if its only for pennies. What a lot of new traders fail to understand is that it is better to limit your risk/exposure.

Of course, this is just my humble opinion and I'll continue to approach my trading in this way.

I would highly recommend the book "Trading in the Zone". You must try at least 15 trades of a system before you start changing. --- 帖子 #520 ---
Ron,

I noticed the same thing on my AskFX EA. Two trades open and closed at the same price. The EA worked well though all winners.

One other thing to look at. If you do not enter a trade on the first day the signal is available or if you reach TP, this EA will re-enter the same trade (if the signal condition is still valid). The EA does not check how many days the valid signal has existed before placing an order.

I observed the re-entry after a TP condition during back tests.

Edit: I forgot to mention that when the EA is modified to let one trade run until the AO changes color it also helps the re-entry problem.

I attached my statement, log files, and the EA I am using (the most recent version) below so you can see my settings.

As per your rules, do we not wait for the close of the signal candle and start of new candle b4 we enter the trade?

--- 帖子 #598 ---
Because many different brokers have different starting times, and price feeds as well.

FXDD and FxPro servers are at GMT+3 both, but FXDD doesn't have a sunday candle. Both start the day at 21:00 GMT.

ODL and IBFX are at GMT+0 and start the day at 00:00 GMT.

Alpari is at GMT+1, I think. And so on.

--- 帖子 #653 ---
I think it can make a large difference in the daily signals. Having a platform that includes an extra day changes mathematical calculations. Even two platforms with server times of GMT+3 can have different weekly opening and closing times.

I am surprised that everyone  has not downloaded a FXDD platform so their charts will match Ash's. The best way to learn a system is to compare your own trades with the system's author. There have been many posts related to this. I think the thread would be easier to read and understand if only one broker's charts were discussed and posted.

--- 帖子 #735 ---
Paris I found the post that Ash made regarding the PSAR (This was post 147):

Quote:

Originally Posted by doblece http://www.forexfactory.com/images/buttons/viewpost.gif
It's in the "final points" of the method:

"Please bear in mind that when entering a trade, it doesn't matter in which order the indicators may line up, e.g. the AO and AC don't have to change colour at the same candle as the first PSAR dot appearing. Or perhaps the AO / AC / Stochs might be compliant before the first PSAR dot appears, or vice versa, and this is fine."

What this means is, it doesn't matter which order the AO or AC or Stochs line up... So either AO can come before AC, or vice versa, or AC can come before Stochs or vice versa, or AO can come before Stochs or vice versa. It doesn't matter. But as long as they all line up when the PSAR appears it's cool. I.e. they don't all have to change on the same candle.

What DOES matter is that we only take trades upon the close of the first PSAR dot.

Hope this clarifies things, and apologies for the ambuigity.

--- 帖子 #782 ---
Ok, obviously we hit our first TP of 25 pips very easily, and stop was moved to BE.

Our second lot stands at around 145 pips.

Now, the question is, do we

a) move SL further down to protect our profits?

b) close our position now?

c) just let the system do it's thing with AO?

I know many of you must be thinking it's a good time to close now, or good time to move stop further down, because I know people use my system for entries, yet prefer their own exits, and that's totally fine, it's your trade, and your right to do what you like.

However, for those of you who wanna follow AshFX Daily to the letter, then officially we wait till the AO closes as green.

Yes, it could be that this retraces back up horriby, and we just close for 25 pips profit, but that's the nature of trading.

--- 帖子 #809 ---
Well, I have finished writing my EA this past weekend and have been making little tweaks and fixes here and there.  Naturally through the course of testing the EA has been reloaded several time and for the AUD/JPY has bought lower each time I reset after a change.  It's a valid signal but it brings up questions.

Let me first explain the way the EA works...

Settings

Order01LotSize: 0.1 (Size of first trade and has a TP determined by the EA)
Order02LotSize: 0.1 (Size of second trade and has no TP set when placed)Second trade is close by the EA when conditions according to the AshFX system are met.
MaxDiffFromOpen: 10 (Number of pips difference from open price)If buy then price can't be greater than open +10 pipsAnything less is fair to open
If sell then price can't be less than open -10 pipsAnything greater is fair to open
TakeSSTrades: true (allow second strength trades to be opened)

OrderSlippage: 3 (number of pips the price can differ when placing a trade)

EAMagicNumber: 20080706 (day I wrote the EA and used by EA to determine if a trade belongs to the EA)This number can be used on all currencies the EA is attached to but can't be duplicated on the same currency if 2 charts are open for the same currency pair.
Now for the questions...

1) If you buy lower than the open or sell greater than the open should the TP still be determined by the price you bought or sold at?  In other words, If I was supposed to buy at 100.25 with a TP at 100.50 but I actually bought at 100.15 then should my TP still be 100.50 or should it be 100.40.The system bases it's decision upon the close of the last bar/open of the current bar so I'm inclined to set SL and TP based on the numbers they're supposed to be.  If you should happen to get in at a lower price then your TP would be larger and the SL smaller for a long position.  The 'MaxDiffFromOpen' variable was put into place to give you the power to say how far off the price could move and still place a trade.  This way if you started the EA at an off time for whatever reason you wouldn't accidentally place trades on a bar that had all the right signals but had already ran a great deal up into the possible profit.
2) On the attached chart I have added a custom indicator I had from a while back (Support and Resistance (Barry)).  Has anyone used this indicator or feel that it is showing valuable/accurate information?  I need something that can be looked at by the EA without my manual intervention that could determine support/resistance.  This may also be useful for possibly taking a trade but with a lower TP if support/resistance is slightly against your full TP determined by the system.  Maybe a new setting for the EA not to trade for less than X pips to prevent very small trades.

I have also attached a EUR/AUD image showing the S/R.  If I had utilized the indicator then I might have set a lower TP and been out already.  At one point I had roughly 80+ pips and is now riding around -119 pips.  The TP is set for 1.6163 (187 pips) but I might have taken 80+ knowing the S/R levels before placing the trade.

As a side note on the EUR/AUD...  According to the AshFX system all the signals were in line for this trade and the SL is still a ways off.  This could very well still be a good trade or it could have been one of those trades people avoided due to the Support level not allowing for the full TP.  Again this is where validating the Support and Resistance of the indicator shown would be helpful.  Does it look accurate?

--- 帖子 #810 ---
Actually, as I think about it, it's probably better if you can buy lower or sell high to have a TP based on the price you actually bought or sold at.  This way you might have a better chance with the second trade riding the wave since the update to break even would be lower for a long and higher for a short.  This is not to say that I would intentionally try to get in lower or higher but if that happens to be the case then so be it.  I will keep the TP based on where I actually bought or sold.

Example (make believe trade below):

The AshFX system determines a 50 pip TP based on the signals/bar values.

It also suggests you buy at say 100.25 (100.75 would be TP)

However, due to conditions (maybe between close on Friday and open on Sunday or something else) you actually buy at 100.15.  In this case the EA would set the TP to 100.65 (still 50 pips) also making the update to break even on the 2nd position lower (100.15 rather than 100.25).

Thoughts?

--- 帖子 #861 ---
The TP is outlined in the PDF.  If long then Close - Low of signal bar and if Short then High - Close.

CAD/JPY is 103.11 (swing low) because it's a second strength trade.  The Stoch was over 50 and below 80.  If it were below the 50 then the SL would have been the Low of the bar that signaled the trade (104.60).  You have the wrong SL set.

--- 帖子 #862 ---

--- 帖子 #863 ---
You're not using the FXDD Demo, you're using ODL.  That's why your data feed is different.  Thats one problem.  You're also not using the standard PSAR indicator that comes with MetaTrader.  This is also a problem.  Check out the PSAR in Ash screenshots, then look at yours.

So, get FXDD, install it, and load the template from page 1 of this thread.  Don't do anything other than that.

If you're using FXDD with the standard indicators that come with it then you will get exactly the same charts and signals as Ash.  This is because you will be getting the same data feed (FXDD) as he is with the same indicators(STANDARD) as he is.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #864 ---
Here is the EA for anyone who would like to test it.  Remember I only wrote it this past weekend and may not have all the bugs worked out.  It's also programmed to only run on demo accounts for right now and I would strongly suggest using FXDD since other brokers vary so much.

Here is a repeat explanation of the settings...

Attach the EA to a Daily chart.

Settings

Order01LotSize: 0.1 (Size of first trade and has a TP determined by the EA)
Order02LotSize: 0.1 (Size of second trade and has no TP set when placed)Second trade is closed by the EA when conditions according to the AshFX system are met (AO changes color).
MaxDiffFromOpen: 10 (Number of pips difference from open price)If buy then price can't be greater than open +10 pipsAnything less is fair to open
If sell then price can't be less than open -10 pipsAnything greater is fair to open
TakeSSTrades: true (allow second strength trades to be opened)

OrderSlippage: 3 (number of pips the price can differ when placing a trade)

EAMagicNumber: 20080706 (day I wrote the EA and used by EA to determine if a trade belongs to the EA)This number can be used on all currencies the EA is attached to but can't be duplicated on the same currency if 2 charts are open for the same currency pair.

Thanks for everyone's support.

--- 帖子 #887 ---
I don't put any faith in backtesting even if 90% modeling quality.  I was recently backtesting another EA which is the first I had done in a long time and thought I would try it again.  What I found was that the strategy tester has some huge flaws.  I would run thru the visual mode as slow as I could handle watching and found that stop losses and take profits weren't always honored.  If the price went 1 pip past but didn't actually land on the TP or SL then it was ignored.  This is a big problem and something that can throw a big monkey wrench into your testing.  At least with live trading you would hope the broker honors your TPs and SLs and closes them when they should even if the price doesn't land directly on your target.  To each his/her own.  I just don't believe backtesting is accurate enough to put any stock into it.

--- 帖子 #888 ---

--- 帖子 #889 ---
The EA does more than just open trades.  You have to leave it open or it won't work right.  The EA manages the trades once they are placed.

1) Update to break even on second position once TP of first is hit.

2) Close 2nd trade once AO changes color.

No EA can do this if it's not running any more than a computer can do a virus scan if it's powered off.

The EA sets a boolean (True/False) variable to true once the trades are placed and looks to make sure it doesn't duplicate trades on the same day.  If you close the EA then all variables would revert back to their default values and the EA thinks it needs to do something.  I can write extra code to check for live trades first but this shouldn't happen if you leave it running.  Besides, once it passes the initial trigger date then it wouldn't see a trade anymore but it still needs to be running.

The idea of running an Expert adviser is that it handles the trades so you don't have to but you need to let it do it's job.

I'm perhaps stressing this more than need be but so many people still don't understand how an EA really works and they really need to if they intend to use them.  Please don't take it the wrong way.

--- 帖子 #893 ---
MagicNumber: The unique trade identification number for this EA. This allows the EA to figure out which trades it is supposed to manage.

SignalMail: If you set up metatrader for e-mail, it will send e-mails to you whenever a trade occurs.

EachTickMode: If set to true, the EA will look for a trade every tick, and place the trade as soon as the signal appears. If set to false, the EA will look for a trade ONLY AT THE CLOSE OF A BAR.

--- 帖子 #894 ---
You will notice a balance of $49,964.00.  This is because of trades I closed manually while making some changes yesterday before I posted the EA here.  I didn't reset the account because I would have lost the AUD/JPY trades from the day before and the EA wouldn't replace them because the signal had passed the day before.

I am not seeing double trades or any other problems right now like others but I have not shut down the EA/platform and am leaving it run like it should.  You will also notice the 2nd orders have the TP as their comment whereas the 1st order is Order1.  This is how the EA distinguishes the trades.  The 2nd order with no TP looks at it's comment to see it the SL should be moved to break even.

--- 帖子 #977 ---
Noticed that AUD/USD closed first position and didn't update the 2nd to break even.  I have corrected the problem and also added support to check for opne trades first before placing new ones.  This way when you shut down MT4 and reopen after copying the new EA it will not replace new trades.

It is still important to leave MT4, the charts, and the attached EA running 24/7 because it does the trading for you.  It requires the software to be running for this to happen.

Should be safe for anyone running the old EA to replace with new one.

1) Close MT4

2) Copy new EA to Expert directory

3) Open MT4

Comment on chart should read "AshFX AutoTrader v1.0c"

--- 帖子 #1049 ---
SS means "Second Strength" (explained in the manual), hence you place your stop at the "swing low" or "swing high".  By swing, we mean the last major turning point.

Look at my pics, the blue line is where the Swing Low or Swing High is, i.e. where I have placed my stops.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1094 ---
Neither...

For qualified everything needs to be red on the first PSAR.

For SS, then only AO can be green.  Because the AC is green on first PSAR then it isn't SS either.

Doesn't matter where Stochs are.  It's already broken the AC rules for both types of entry.  On qualified it breaks the AC rule, and on SS it breaks the AC rule.  Only AO can be green for SS trade.

Don't get me wrong, I'm just looking at what the manual says.

--- 帖子 #1176 ---
First, thanks for your support.

I agree and am currently looking for a possible indicator that the EA could look at for S/R values and determine if trade should still be made.  I have expressed this earlier in the thread.

The EA looks for the right signal and if found makes the trade.  That trade could happen at any time during the whole daily bar.  Of course there is a value (10 by default) that prevents the EA from buying too high from the open or selling too low.  Once a trade is made then it knows it's done it's job and keeps that in memory as long as it remains running.  If you then close the trade manually and reopen the system then of course it's going to want to trade again.  A suggestion would be to turn off live trading on the EA if you don't want it to trade that day but your kind of wanting to mix manual decisions with an automated system.  An S/R indicator would help if it's reliable.

Keep in mind you can also tell the EA not to trade Second Strength trades in the settings.

Perhaps you should trade these manually.  This EA is not closed to discussion for enhancements but it was originally written to follow the system rules at least for now.  Sounds like you may make decisions on-the-fly based on what you "feel" at that time.  These types of things can be very complicated for EA's since a "human" on-the-fly decision can be more complicated than some people realize and then it all needs to be "hard coded" into the EA.

Any pair you open a chart for and attach the EA to it.

Trade only is possible but not manage only.  Well, it can be but I'm not interested in the work to manage only.  When an EA doesn't place it's own trades it has no idea which trades it should/shouldn't manage.  It may end up altering trades you didn't intend it to manage.  Things can be done with comments (EA tracks down trades with specific comments) but it gets sloppy.  When an EA is programmed correctly the programmer gives the orders a magic number value.  That value is the looked for when looping through the trades along with the symbol and maybe even a specific comment for the order.  When you place a manual order you can't give it a magic number.

If you want everything the exact same then you can get one chart set exactly how you want it and then save it as a template.  You can then apply that template to any of your other charts.  You will have to set the initial template for each MT4 install or copy the template file to the other locations.

So would I but the I can see potential problems with that as well, especially if your running various other EAs that you may not want changed as well.  As far as I know there is no way to do this.

--- 帖子 #1187 ---
What I meant is that while placing the trade manually you can't enter a magic number.  Through an EA I can put magic numbers on open trades/pending trades all day long.  My point was that you would still need a way to distinguish which trades should actually be hijacked by the EA.  You may not want it to grab all but only certain ones.  One way would be to enter a unique comment and then have the EA look for that as it loops through the trades but I feel that can have it's own problems.

I'm not saying it would happen but if someone forgot to add the comment, mistyped the comment, etc. then they could end up in trouble because the EA might not find the right match.  I have used comments as a way to monitor/manage trades and in fact I do that with this EA.  Second order's comment is the TP of the first.  This way if the EA is interrupted or the first order stops out, etc. I can still get the information needed to know when to update to break even.  But in my EA I know exactly what to expect in the comment and it also has the symbol and magic number confirming I have the right trade.  The EA will not mistype my comment.

I know it seems like I'm going on but I feel it's important for us all to understand at least a bit.  This is also not meant to discourage or say something can't be done.  If I can enlighten some on the mysteries behind an EA than they may also be able to translate to me what they want and how they think it may work.

I always read more into what people may ask of me because I'm used to digging for what they really want.  If someone asks me for a donut then I can guess that they'll also want coffee (2 creams / 1 sugar), a plate, spoon, napkin, etc.  At this point I need you (whoever) to be as specific as possible.  Seeing the whole picture initially reduce fixes, work arounds, kinks, etc.

Hello mtaboneweb

By using the script that I am refering to one may place an order manually and assign a magic number to the order. Then the trader could assign any EA which has magic number capabilities to manage the trade. This would be best done only if the EA could be set to 'manage only' so it wouldn't buy or sell additional orders.

Whether or not you wish to modify your EA to have a 'manage only' mode is totally up to you of course, I just thought I would share the fact that it is possible to manually enter a trade and assign a magic number.

I have tested this script and it seems to work. I entered a buy, lot size, and magic number. I then attached an EA with the same magic number set to manage trades only. There are two other open trades on the account but the EA is only seeing the one that the magic number was assigned to using the script.

Attached File(s)   OpenMagic.mq4

|
484 downloads

Attached File(s)   OpenMagic.ex4

3 KB
|
355 downloads

To use this script place it in your experts/scripts folder. To manually open a trade with a magic number just double click on the script then choose buy or sell, lot size, and assign a magic number.

Happy trading. . .

--- 帖子 #1205 ---
Hi mtaboneweb,

I would like to offer some help re. identifying possible S/R Zones.

There are a number of papers available free on the net re. Drummond Geometry. One of the aspects of this system is the identification of potential S/R Zones through the use of MTF 3 Moving Averages High, Low, & Typical Price.

Currently I'm using the attached #MTF_Moving Average indicator as follows;

Whatever time frame you choose to trade, attach three MTF 3 MA's (High, Low, & Typical Price) for each time frame greater than the one you have chosen to trade - My preference is to skip the next higher TF.

For example;

Trading H1: Open MTF 3 MA's (High, Low, & Typical Price) for each Daily (1440), Weekly (10080) & Monthly (43200)
Trading H4: Open MTF 3 MA's (High, Low, & Typical Price) for each Weekly (10080) & Monthly (43200)
Trading D: Open MTF 3 MA's (High, Low, & Typical Price) for Monthly (43200), this indicator will not show Quarterly so I have to be manually calculate them - If someone can fix this Great!!!

For visual reasons, I'm using an easy to follow colour coding system for each, e.g. High - Red, Low - Blue, & Typical Price - White. I also use different line styles or thickness for each TF.

These MTF MA's identify Possible S/R Zones, obviously there may be some slippage either side of the line.

Hope this helps

--- 帖子 #1225 ---
I wanted more information on the PSAR. Thought I would share it.   Big E

Parabolic SAR
Parabolic SAR provides a useful tool for catching new trends early, offering excellent buy and sell signals.
Overview <LI class=EducationIndexTXT>The Parabolic SAR (stop and reverse) is a trend-following system that sets "stop-losses." <LI class=EducationIndexTXT>It works well in trending markets, but tends to whipsaw during non-trending, sideways phases. <LI class=EducationIndexTXT>A parabola below the price is generally bullish. A parabola above the price is generally bearish. http://www.chartfilter.com/reports/c31_files/c31-1.gifThe Parabolic System, developed by Welles Wilder who also developed the Relative Strength Index (RSI), is usually referred to as the Parabolic "SAR" (stop-and-reverse). Mr Wilder designed this indicator to supplement the other trend-following systems.

The Parabolic SAR is a "stop-loss" system used to set trailing price stops. The name of the system is derived from its parabolic shape, which follows the price movements in the form of a dotted line. When the parabola follows along below the price, the trader should be buying or going long. A parabola above the price suggests selling or going short.

The particular value of the Parabolic SAR is that it allows traders to catch new trends relatively early. If the new trend fails, the parabola quickly switches from one side of the price to the other, thus generating the stop and reverse signal.

Mr. Wilder built an acceleration factor into the Parabolic system. To allow the trend time to become established, the movement of the indicator starts off slowly - with the dots close together. As acceleration increases, the parabola move faster (with the dots further apart) until it catches up to the price action.

As with most indicators, Parabolic SAR performs best in trending markets, and is less reliable during sideways or congestive phases.
Signals

The Parabolic SAR is an outstanding indicator for providing exit points - offering sell signals when the parabola moves above the price. Buy signals are generated when the parabola falls below the price. Of course, these signals need to be confirmed by the price action itself and other, complementary indicators.

It is always useful to examine different time periods; using daily, weekly and monthly charts.
Combining Parabolic SAR with DMI

John Murphy, author of Technical Analysis of the Financial Markets, recommends using a filter to complement the Parabolic system. He suggests using the Directional Movement Index (DMI) to help eliminate whipsaws and false signals in the more sensitive Parabolic system. As a simple rule of thumb, he observes that the DMI and Parabolic SAR indicators can complement one another as follows: "When the +DI line is above the -DI line, all Parabolic sell signals can be ignored." We can see the effectiveness of this strategy below. (The ADX line is essentially the smoothed difference between the +DI and -DI lines.)http://www.chartfilter.com/reports/c31_files/c31-2.gif

--- 帖子 #1284 ---
Hello everyone!

I have followed this thread for weeks and receive Ash's alerts. I see that there are some that let their emotions get the best of them and stay out of the game. I have read a lot on the technichal and fundamentals of trading and the biggest thing that I have taken from all of it is no matter how good a system is, it comes down to your emotions. I have taken many trades and as soon as it moved against me, I would get nervous and exit the trade to find out hours later it went my way!

So, I would suggest reading about the mental state of trading and possibly looking at finding a time frame that works best for your trading style. I also drill down to smaller time frames for entry and comfirmation along with using  Fibs, and candle recognition.

I took the GBP/USD long trade.

Happy trading

--- 帖子 #1333 ---
To ASH's point just entering a trade because all the indicators line up is risky without other considerations. With that said if you are mechanically trading this way or on auto with an EA your win lose ratio will be marginal. Trader discretion considering candle patterns, support and resistance as well as fundamentals are all worth considering before taking a postion. Knowing when not to trade is a discipline that takes time and patience to master. If it were as easy as just jumping in and setting SL and TP this would be the holy grail and we would not need anything else. There is no Holy Grail but your own ability to master the space between your ears and develop your individual trading style that works for you. Thanks Ash again for Pipnailer and the Daily system which by using I have gotten alot farther down the road in becoming successfull at this.

--- 帖子 #1352 ---
The signal bar would be yesterday's bar. Both the Stoch main line and Stoch signal line are above the 50 level on that bar. I opened the data window to confirm. That is why Ash identified it as a first strength trade. In the PDF Ash speaks of the Stochs in a plural tense so both lines would have to be above 50.

If you are talking about the blue line on the Stoch that is the Stoch main line with the red line being the Stoch signal line. If you are talking about the blue line on your main chart, I would guess it is a moving average. We don't have that line on the default template so I don't know. If you press Ctrl+I or right-mouse-click on your chart and select 'indicator list' from the drop down menu you will be able to determine what the chart blue line is.

--- 帖子 #1358 ---
Greetings . . . this is my first full week of experimenting with AshFX.

OzFX did exceptionally well with the use of the EA or manually for about 2-3 months. After that, though, my results were spotty to say the least on both 4H and Daily trades. I was intrigued by the multiple confirmations used in the AshFx system to validate a trade, so it seemed worth a serious look. So far, so good.

OzFX was my first experience using an EA, and I would be hesitant to try it again with this system. Ash has addressed the need to be aware of S & R before entering a trade, and I agree completely. An EA only determines that the rules of the system have been met, and that may be enough at times, but I personally believe that adding trader discretion to a good system will enhance it even further.

That's a turnabout from what I often said on the OzFX thread, but I learned a valuable lesson over time that an EA may work well, even for extended periods, but it does not and should not replace the trader completely.

With a system based on Daily charts, such as AshFX, trading manually should not be a major issue anyway. That's just my view . . . for those who want to try an EA with this system, I hope it works well for you.

--- 帖子 #1371 ---
Hi guys,

I had something that I needed to get perfectly clear, that's caused me some needless losses because I was mistaken.

In Ash's .pdf manual it says, concerning the exit rules for First Strength Trades:

"As for taking profit, then there are two methods of exiting that should be used together. The first TP is equivalent to the same number of pips as the SL. So, for example, if your SL is 100 pips, then your first TP would also be 100 pips. Once this TP is hit you will close half your position AND you set your SL to breakeven."

The problem I have had on some of the trades is that I was stopped out early when I shouldn't have been. One thing I did wrong on a trade was that I set the initial TP at 100 pips from the entry price when the SL was about 200 pips away. Then I moved the SL to breakeven and the price promptly retraced and stopped me out. (For some reason the number 100 stuck in my mind  ) From now on I'll set the inital TP at the same pips as the SL.

About moving the SL to breakeven after the first TP is hit, I understand that. But what is the best way to proceed after that? Is it best to leave it there until the AO changes color, (the exit price) or would it be safer to trail it down behind some level like the high (low) of the previous day's candle to lock in profits in the event that price makes a strong retracement against you?

What is anyone's thoughts on this?

Thanks.

--- 帖子 #1372 ---
I'm sure with practice you do not need to use the data window. I used it to make a point. You can always use the data window to check the settings on a previous bar if you do not trust your eyes or want to know why an EA traded the way it did.

The key is you are checking the signal bar and if there is a valid signal, and you think it would be a good trade, you would open it close to the beginning of a new FXDD daily bar.

--- 帖子 #1413 ---
Todays candle is not the issue and is not important. Your decision should be based on the candle where the first PSAR changed.

For AudNzd for candle of 16/07:

PSAR flipped to top - Good for short trade

Candle is red - Good for short trade

Stochs above 50 - Good for First Strength trade

AC is green - NOT Good for short trade

AO is red - Good for short trade

Only problem is AC is the wrong colour. When todays candle opened it doesn't matter what colour it is and will probably change many times as price fluctuates. Your decision should be based on the candle where the PSAR first flipped. Obviously you may want to watch the price action on the new day to make your final decision.

This is my understanding of the rules.

--- 帖子 #1414 ---
38.2% and 61.8% (basic reversal points) are symmetric. 50% will always be 50% either way.

So really it shouldn't matter how do you draw it, and many always take the 0% for swing low and 100% for swing high points, independently if we are evaluating the possible pullback from a rise or a fall.

And even "logically",  you can see it both ways: for example, if price rises from, say, 1.9800 to 1.9900 and pulls back to 1.9862, it will have pulled back 38% of the total 100 pips move. So we draw it from low to high. But, it will also be at 62% of the total move, and thus we can draw it from high to low. It will depend on how you usually handle the data.

I prefer the first option (measuring from the START of the move to the END of the move), and if we want to use additional values I find it is more accurate, but I've been getting accustomed to draw it like in the second one (always the same, swing low 0% and swing high 100%) because it is much faster. Because in the end, what matters is the area where it will probably reach tp or reverse, independently of the number or name we assign to it.

--- 帖子 #1422 ---
Hi Dave,

Once first T/P is hit you have a number of options where to place your stop  loss

1. when AO changes colour and then close at end of candle

2. nearest support or resistance points

3. nearest fib levels

4 nearest swing high or low

I suggest you google Baby Pips or any of the above and then get to understand what your money risk is to what you are prepared to lose to win in the end

By the way i would not trade GB/JP - too volatile for me

Paul

--- 帖子 #1466 ---
the adx is called average directional movement index in mt4. I dont know much about it but it measures the strength of a trend.  The blue line or solid line lets you know how strong the trend is by how high it is, and the dotted lines let you know what direction the trend is going.

--- 帖子 #1471 ---
I have read in another forum that in general the longer the timescale the lower the ADX period. As for any other indicator, I think this is a setting you might experiment with and analyze which period is better or more accurate.

The                              +DI indicates the up average.
The                              -DI indicates the down average.
The                              ADX, average directional movement index, shows                              whether a trend is in effect by smoothing the                              difference between the +DI and -DI. It shows the momentum over the last "x" bars of the timescale in view.

An ADX of 14 periods will be taking into account the last 14 bars, be it days, hours or minutes.

--- 帖子 #1475 ---
Here is how I trade AshFx :

I use the low/high of the signal candle as Stop Loss (SL)

Use the same number of pips as "virtual" Take Profit (TP)

If this SL/TP is more than 150 pips I use 150 pips

I put a Trailing Stop (TS) of 50 pips when i enter the trade.

(better safe than sorry, i hate to see my trade go +50 pips to finally hit my SL )

At half the TP i close half of the trade and let the other part run until it reach TS or...

When it reach TP i change my TS to 25 pips and let it run until it close by itself.

Also I do not care much about the stoch level as soon as it is in the same way as the trade

I use MT4 alerts to know when Half TP or TP is reached.

For the moment it has been working quite good:

Today I entered a buy for

GBPCHF       GBPJPY       AUDJPY       CADJPY

One of these wasn't a valid AshFx signal (AUDJPY i think)  but I realised that too late.

GBPCHF +2 (hit TS)

GBPJPY +28 (hit TS)

CADJPY closed half at +57

Still running are

CADJPY part 2 down to +45 for now

AUDJPY +26

Hope this helps...

--- 帖子 #1485 ---
You can change the settings on the parameter's tab in the Stoch's property box. You can bring up the properties box several ways. One way would be to right mouse click on your chart and select 'indicators list' from the drop down menu. Select the Stochastic Oscillator  from the indicators list and press edit. You can also change the setting when you attach an indicator to the chart or sometimes by right clicking on the indicator.

--- 帖子 #1487 ---
Go to MT4 trading station, find Indicators folder (under Accounts), open it.

Find Scochastic Oscillator, double click it, set your numbers on it, it will attach itself to the chart window.

Very easy, so good luck!

Oh! you want to be able to tell which is indicator Slow stochastic:

(Check it out, I hope this one is going to help you.)

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_oscillator

--- 帖子 #1488 ---
Also note that the indicator is set to slowing by default so all u need do is alter the periods in the parameter tab.Click ok and your are done.

Hope it works for you

--- 帖子 #1624 ---
Remember that all indicators' values are based on the price. As the current bar's price is constantly changing, so is the value of the indicator for that bar. What you see in visual backtesting is the final value of the indicator at the close of a bar, you don't know what that indicator looked like at the start of the bar.

--- 帖子 #1627 ---
RR gave you a good idea of why you need to wait until the candle is complete to determine where the PSAR dot will stay for sure.

In regard to why it may be better to wait and follow the AshFX rules, the idea of a system like this is to allow you to get into the “meat” of a trend, that is, when the trend has picked up some steam and you can still enjoy some good returns.

A number of other trading systems will try to identify the breakout of a trend right from the start, but you will probably find that your win/loss percentage is much lower on systems like that. It’s easy to look back at AshFX signals and say “I could have gotten even more pips”, but you will generally find that your trade signals are more reliable and profitable on a system like this.

I'm actually a U.S. expatriate living in Guanajuato, Mexico. I speak passable Spanish, but I'm far from fluent. Any attempts, though, to speak Spanish here are warmly received by the residents, so I'm slowly adding to the vocabulary.

Thanks for taking the time to create this thread. I was a wholehearted supporter of the OzFX system and did really well with it for several months, but things seemed to change overnight and the results became much more hit and miss.

As Ronald Raygun noted, for those of us who traded OzFX, your system seems somewhat like a "cousin". There's some definite similarities, but I like the additional safeguards built into AshFX to prevent getting into questionable trades. And, you've been honest enough to stress the need to take a good look at S & R before entering a trade, which will help traders to actually learn to trade instead of blindly following every signal. Your suggested MM, in my opinion, is also a vast improvement over the OzFX system.

So far, I've been very impressed with the AshFX system, so thanks again, or perhaps I should say "Muchisimas gracias. Lo agredezco.

Hi, Could someone please help me with this: Does the PSAR change it's position once it has appeared on top or under a candle? (forgive me if this is a repeated question)

--- 帖子 #1722 ---
The current PSAR can change its position during the course of a trading day, which is why trading decisions are made when the daily candle is complete. Once a daily candle is complete, though, the PSAR dot remains as it was.

--- 帖子 #1737 ---
This is not a long trade I would take at current price levels for a couple of reasons:

1. Significant resistance at around 0.9840 that has held for the last few weeks. We both marked an uptrend line on our charts, but price action has definitely stalled at the resistance area.

2. This pair is at a record high. The Momentum indicator is not part of the AshFX system, but I do take a look at it, and we're clearly seeing evidence of reduced momentum on both Daily and Weekly charts.

The really nice long trade opportunities began several months ago at the start of 2008. Since then, price has climbed about 1200 pips. Now that I'm seeing a lot of resistance, I'm not sure I want to jump on a Long signal just in hopes that the pair will continue to climb.

The one factor that would probably cause me to enter this trade, and it would be based on technical trading rather than AshFX rules, would be if I saw a significant break of the resistance area. If that happened, I would look for a retrace back to the previous resistance area and then place a Long trade with a fairly tight stop loss assuming that this area would now become a support zone.

That's my take on how I would handle it. That's the great thing about trading. It's like looking at art . . . everyone has a slightly different perspective on what they're seeing. If a signal comes, and you decide to take the trade, good luck and I'll be cheering you on from the sidelines. On the other hand, if a valid short signal shows up soon on this pair, I'll be all over that. The retracement possibilities look sweet.

--- 帖子 #1814 ---
I've been testing a couple of filters for the signal candle to try and block bad trades:

1) Don't take doji candle signals. i.e short signal candle body equals no trade.

2) If the distance between the signal psar and the signal candle wick is greater than the candles high-low, then don't take that either.  This will help to remove a lot of the trades where the stop is going to be substantially larger than the target profit.

These modifications will block a few good trades too, but they will block many more false signals where you are either getting whipsawed or taking huge risk for a possibly small profit.

3) I've also been using MTF HAS on a 15 min chart.  It shows 15m, 30m, 1hr, and 4hr.  If going long, then after the signal candle wait for the 15m and 30m HAS to close green.   Wait for reds for a short.   This is a way of getting in at a better time after the retracement that often occurs following the signal candle.  That's if you've got time to keep an eye on it.

Check with FXDD. When I funded my account a few months ago, they just wanted to see 150 trades in whatever type of account you opened (standard, mini, or micro).

I use MetaTrader. I'm not sure why you would want to switch platforms each time you trade, but my suggestion would be to contact FXDD with that question.

I'm not saying this is a losing system or anything (in fact it should be quite profitable) but since we are on the topic of people posting their pips and all, I will say this: I've noticed on forexfactory no one likes to brag about their losses, everyone always brags about how many pips they make. who wants to brag about losing money? so of course on every single thread here you will only see positive comments (mostly) saying how they made X pips today or this week.. but a few months later you don't see them anymore.

--- 帖子 #1863 ---

--- 帖子 #1864 ---
You need to download a MT4 demo from FXDD. Save the template file (AshFX_Daily.tpl) from the first post to the template folder. Then after re-starting MT4 apply the template file to your charts. Brokers that have a Sunday bar or different opening times will show different signals. Having a Sunday bar creates a 6 day week with one day showing very little movement. This can effect mathimatical calculations. Since Ash created and tested his system on FXDD it is a good idea to learn the system on that demo. It also helps so you can compare trades with others in the thread. You can have MT4 platforms from more than one broker on your computer. If you compare a couple of them every day you will see the difference. It is always possible that another platform with modified parameters may work just as well or better. Time will tell.

A specific broker's server times are the same in every country. An FXDD account will have the same server time and the chart will display the same everywhere in the world. The PSAR settings are in the first post. "Parabolic Stop and Reverse (PSAR, 0.03, 0.2)"

--- 帖子 #1868 ---
Hi Everyone,

Interesting to see that there has been some talk about the profitability of this system and the money management aspect. I would like to throw in my thoughts and I am interested what others think.

I have monitored the system rigorously during July and, if the rules were strictly adhered to, then the system is in loss. Looking at the trades I believe the reason for this is the risk to reward for second strength trades. Have a look back to 9th July at GBP/CHF and AUD/CAD and also 15th July to EUR/CHF, EUR/JPY and USD/JPY to see heavily losing trades. Those trades alone could have lost in excess of 1200 pips and indeed you would double that for the two lots that the system suggests are risked for each trade - 2400+ pips!

Now, if winning trades, massively outnumber those that lose and the second part of the trade runs on to a big win then that may not be a problem. However, quite often the second trade reverts to the break even stop loss. So, the profit is the first lot only which generally is a lot less than the risk.

Now, it may be that July is not a representative month. And, I should add, I have not given up on the system because of July's results. However, I am adopting a more conservative money management strategy for the second strength trades (see the post by AIRX3000 for further details earlier in the thread) whilst still monitoring the trades against the system that Ash designed. It could be that future months may be fine.

One final thing I would add is that I wouldn't rely on any of the EA's results just yet. As far as I am aware none of them have been tested enough to suggest that they are error free and, as such, I don't think anyone should be basing their trading strategy on them (apologies to those guys writing the EA's - I am sure that they will be of great benefit in the future).

Just my thoughts, I may not be infallible with my analysis but I thought I would put my point of view for discussion.

--- 帖子 #1869 ---
Your post, IMHO, nicely illustrates the danger of taking any system and putting it on auto-pilot. This system was not meant to totally replace trader discretion. If you look back at previous posts, you will see a number of examples where Ash, the system creator, passed on a trade due to strong support or resistance.

Signals are merely that . . . a signal for each trader to take a look at a currency pair and then make a decision as to whether it's a trade they feel comfortable with. I have only been tracking results for the last couple of weeks, but in that time I have probably taken only about 50% of the AshFX signals. Blending the signal with some discretion has allowed me to earn about 550 pips in that time.

--- 帖子 #1870 ---
Henry Ford said it best: “If you think you can…. or if you think you can’t…you’re right!”

60 years ago, running a 4-minute mile was an "unrealistic goal". 50 years ago, getting a man to the moon was an "unrealistic goal", and so it goes throughout history.

Will you achieve a 10% monthly return? Maybe . . . maybe not. But I think your chances are better if you believe it can be done versus calling it an "unrealistic goal."

--- 帖子 #1873 ---
I agree completely, and that tends to be the trades I stay away from.

I'm using a blend of the two. I tend to take profits on the first lot a little earlier than the rules state. For example, if my first target is 175 pips, I'm usually more than content to put my first lot to bed at 100 pips. By the same token, though, I think it's ill-advised to close out the first lot at 25-30 pips, which I've seen done at times, simply because a system based on Daily charts should be able to generate far more profit that that if it's worthwhile at all.

Likewise, on the second lot, I'm not going to sit by and watch the profits disappear on a trade that's up considerably. At some point, I will cash in on the winnings prior to seeing the trade return to breakeven. For example, on the recent eur/usd short, I was up on the second lot over 200 pips. Price then retraced over 175 pips, and I decided to close the second lot at +100. It has since moved back down, but it ended the day at a previous S & R level, so I'm content with my decision.

--- 帖子 #1874 ---
Im just going to throw my 2 cents in here. Its good read both your points of view, and both of you are on the money. From what I have learned by using the system since July is this 1. If you look at the indicators to tell you when to buy and when to sell, in the long run you will probably end up loosing. I dont look at the indicators to tell me when to trade, I look at it as an invitation to look more into the price action of the pair, such as support, resistance, trends etc.. this is where it becomes discretionary. 2. I have seen all my trades in July hit the profit target on the first lot, only to have all the second lot close at break even. This is where I will listen to Yen's advice and adjust to taking profits on my second trade, whether it is by a trailing stop or just adjusting my stop loss when I am in the green, either way I dont want to be up 200 pips and see it break even 2 days later, that hurts. I had a great month in July, but it would have been that much better if I would have taken profits on the second trade.

I backtested this system for myself over the weekend, on one of the pairs I tested since 2005 out of over 100 trades, only one kept going on the second trade without breaking even first, it made +589 pips. Every other second trade either broke even or closed at very little. Those are not good odds.

Sorry not trying to hijack your conversation, just wanted to share my information.

Hey Gang,

I love the Ash System and it usually makes a profit. That being said, I am retired as a Contractor of 30 years. I love spending the day on my charts every day. I don't use the Ash take profit rules. I exit while in profit and use a predetermined stop that is different for each trade depending upon what I see on the chart, support and resistance, fib., etc. I don't take many losses in any of my trades. By the way, I have seen many posts here where people report any losses... not just profit... but then I read the posts every day. Unless it's mandatory to be away from your computer (i.e.JOB), You shouldn't suffer many losses if your on your charts and know how to read what they are telling you.. If I was gone I would lower my TP in the trade and use a shorter stop loss of about 30 pips. When I'm on the chart and take a 10 pip loss out of existing profit, I'm usually out at that point. If it reverses, it's easy enough for me to get back in and I enjoy the extra pips I saved.  Just my thoughts and strategy. Keep up the good work and posts gang and thanks again Ash.   Eric

You need to be an effective trader to trade the system not a blind follower of the indicators presented. This is a great method as is Pipnailer if traded using one's trading intuition and ability. CAUTION EVERYONE.... I screwed up. On the chart tonight on eur/usd doing some scalping. I always have the order window open on my chart when scalping and check the pair listed. Well this happened twice before I figured it out. I was on FXDD. The order window registered EUR/USD. While waiting for the next candle I scrolled the chart back an hour or so and only looked at the info for 30 seconds at the most... then scrolled back to where the active trade was registering. I saw the buy entry on the chart and took it. about 10 minutes later I closed the trade. I had made about 12 pips. When I went to the History tab... I had lost about 14 Pips. What the hell is going on the burro said...no suds doing this! When I scrolled back to check the chart... it changed the pair on the order window because I was scrolling. I didn't know it would do that... $140 lesson...Ouch! Won't make that mistake again.

Ricki...If I'm on the charts and I'm down 10 pips on an Ash trade... I get out and watch. When and if it turns around I get back in for the rest of the ride. Often saving me 40-60 pips. But remember I'm always monitoring the charts.  Sometimes when I leave the house I'll put a stop loss of 30 pips. And yes, most times I get stopped out. Over the last couple of days... if I leave the house I just close the trade. There is always the next trade coming and it saves me 30 pips loss when I do it that way... I'm not suggesting anyone else do it the same way... but it works for me.

I hope no one looses any pips by screwing up the way I did. Tell the burro I won't do that any more.

Just wanted to post this to help others.   Eric

Again, this may prove to be a decent trade, but I just didn't feel comfortable with it. Trade Update:eur/chf short: 1 lot closed at +50; 2nd lot is now at +39. If this trade can get moving, there's some potential for a decent trade. The lows have been getting lower since 5/9. If you run a fib from 3/17 to the high, the trend line corresponds just about exactly with a 38.2% fib retracement. If you instead run the fib from 4/10 to the high, the trend line corresponds with the 61.8% fib retracement.

Either way, that would bring us to a price of about 1.5975, which would be a cool 300 pips on this trade. Of course, it has a long way to go to hit that target, and both currencies really got clobbered against virtually all other currencies today, so it will be interesting to see if it drops.

I don't see any new AshFX trades that I'm excited about, so it looks like eur/chf will be my only trade going into next week.

--- 帖子 #2025 ---
I think you're correct in every example you mentioned.

Of the four trades you noted, two should never have been taken per AshFX rules. That includes the CHF/JPY trade you mentioned, as well as the AUD/CAD trade. Both were short signals, but each had a bullish signal candle, so neither trade was valid.

If the stop loss rules for a Second Strength trade had been followed, the EUR/JPY trade would not have been stopped out just as you noted. The first lot would have closed at +97 and the second lot would now be about 190 pips up.

The other trade you mentioned was the GBP/CHF short. However, this was never a signal on FXDD charts, which is what Ash recommends for this system (http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=648), so this trade also would not have been taken had that suggestion been heeded.

This isn't meant to cast stones at airx3000 because it's easy to forget details in the heat of trading, but it does illustrate the importance of following the AshFX rules and recommendations to the letter for best results. In this case, it would have prevented some substantial losses.

--- 帖子 #2038 ---
You're asking about a specific company, and I know nothing about them, so I don't feel comfortable answering that question, adeforex.

I will tell you my experience. I did not do well at all trading with pivot points. That doesn't mean there's not any merit to them; I just never felt confident using them. Other traders, conversely, swear by pivot points. You need to find the "shoe" that's comfortable for you. In other words, find a style of trading that fits you and that you will feel comfortable with.

In regard to fib points, my suggestion to you would be to practice and observe how price reacts around the various fib lines, and then incorporate that into your trading style.

In general, I do much better not relying on information provided by outside sources, but that's just my personal opinion. The things I look at in deciding on a trade are strong support and resistance areas, as well as fib and trend lines. I don't make it a lot more complicated than that.

--- 帖子 #2106 ---
GBPCHF I mentioned is not a valid signal. How can I go long or short?

One needs to look at price action as a whole and look for the overall trend direction with S/R and when valid Ashfx signals present then enter the trade.

S/R: trendlines, S/R areas( Use weekly charts for daily charts and draw them ), fibonacci, pivots, 20,50,100,200sma/ema are all valid S/R .Whatever the individual trader feels comfortable !

Do your analysis of price action on the higher timeframe and enter on the lower timeframe. Even exit on a timeframe lower than theone you entered.

Many good exit strategies have been mentioned throughout the thread. A simple one is draw a trendline in the direction of the trade entered and exit when price breaks that trendline.

Hope this helps.

LR

--- 帖子 #2182 ---
I think you should test the system yourself. If you are thinking of trading the system live you will need the practice. I'm sure you don't want to trade real money on a system based on what other people say.

I doubt you will find more than a couple of members that would agree 100% on every trade. (We may come to a consensus by discussing a trade on this thread) The rules look straight forward at first glance until you consider we take support and resistance into the trade decision. There can also be a different view on FS and SS trades. A cross on the stoch can look like a FS trade just viewing it. It can dictate a SS by a small amount if you use the data window to determine the stoch and signal level. Some members even use different brokers like Alpari or IBFX. They will end up with different trades and results. Perhaps with testing they may find a way to more profitable taking the signal from a broker with a day that starts closer to 00:00 GMT. I don't know. I use FXDD because it is the default broker the system was started on.

It is important to trade the system in a way that has proved profitable to you in your forward testing.

--- 帖子 #2185 ---
I totally agree with you. While the strategy looks mechanical and there are several people who have programmed EA's for the strategy, there is definitely a large degree of TRADER"S DISCRETION whether one places the trade or not. This is the S& R zones that traders use which is open for variation. EA's do not pick this up but certainly a great tool to alert you of a possible trade.
Money management is an area too which comes under TRADER"S DISCRETION too.(TRAILING STOPS: USE PSAR TO TRAIL, OR FIXED NUMBER OF PIPS TO TRAIL, FIXED STOPLOSS to give a few variations).

LR

--- 帖子 #2186 ---
If you are talking about the *.tpl file, that is a template file. It is used by MetaQuotes' Metatrader 4. It is a trading platform that is available for free as a demo platform.

You do not open the *.tpl file. Just save it to your computer. Save it to the c:\program files\FXDD - Metatrader4\templates folder. Re-start the platform and right mouse click on your chart and select template and choose the file you saved. (This is one of several ways to apply a template.)

The chart timer is an indicator file you would save it to the c:\program files\FXDD - Metatrader4\experts\indicators folder. You can attach it to the chart from the MT4 navigator window or other ways.

Note: your folder name will vary if you do not use FXDD for your demo account or if you install the MT4 program to a non-standard directory.

--- 帖子 #2240 ---
1. GO to FILE.

2. SAVE picture as...

3.ACTIVE CHART ......Save on desktop (Is the easiest) with a description of your choice so you can findit easily.

Then...

When you post on the forum:

1.Scroll further down to ADDITIONAL OPTIONS

2.Attach Files..... Manage attachments

3. BROWSE....PICK up image from the place you saved your picture(DESKTOP) and ..

4.PRESS UPLOAD.

5.There is place for 2 attachments at a time.

6. If more than 2 charts, repeat steps again.

7.Then press SUBMIT REPLY further down.

Hope this helps

LR

--- 帖子 #2257 ---
GBPUSD is still  not a valid trade on FXDD platform(recommended broker as it does not have a SUNDAY CANDLE). Should not have entered the trade.

The rest are all SS trades. The direction of EURUSD,AUDUSD,GBPUSD is UP,  USDCHF and USDJPY is SHORT.

Depending on your leverage and account balance, if your account can handle it lower or higher your stops. The trades should make profit. Yes the drawdown is high because it is the daily TF.

If either of the stochastic lines are above or below 50 line it is considered an SS trade.( This is my understanding). STOPLOSS placement according to manual.

LR

--- 帖子 #2258 ---
You are right, but with all these trades the weekly charts are the reverse, so we are counter trend trading,

--- 帖子 #2259 ---
Perfectly correct, They are all countertrend trades for the weekly TF. Being daily charts and most of these moves were large, these particular countertrends are expected to at least 38% retracement of the move. Even maybe 50% or 61.8% retracement.Therefore for the aggressive trader, these will translate into many pips.

Some traders trade countertrends, others will trade lower timeframes eg. swingtraders will look at the daily charts for the trend and trade 1h/30m charts in the direction of the daily trend.

It depends on the trading plan for the individual trader and the TF they choose to trade.

Ashfx signals work best on daily TF but will translate to pips in the lower TF.

Several traders use Ashfx as signals with other filters.

LR

Hi All,

I am also in very high negative pips with the Aud/Usd & Eur/Usd so lets see what happens next week

Talking about filters what about one that i nicked from another forum and if i would have had this indicator on both the Au/us & Eu/Us i would not have taken the trade

Open up an RSI indicator window with default settings then darg the willaims percentage indicator on top of the RSI window again with default settings

Make sure that the williams % is applied to previuous indicators data and thats it

When the willaims % range crossing over and above the RSI then go long and visa versa, obviosly usibg R/S & trendlines etc

I am trying it this next couple of weeks to see what it does

Thanks

--- 帖子 #2298 ---
The PSAR does not re-paint.

I'm not sure what broker's chart you are showing but it does not look like a new day has started. The psar dot can change back and forth until the day closes. The server/chart time on any broker's MT4 platform will only agree with the local time in one time zone of the world. For example FXDD the default MT4 charts we use in this thread will not start a new day for another 2 hours and 15 minutes from the time of this post. Which is GMT +3. Until then the dot, along with the AC, AO, and Stoch may continue to change.

--- 帖子 #2299 ---
psar does not repaint. However, if the range of the bar is big enough in each direction, thats just the way it is.

--- 帖子 #2300 ---
Hi

The PSAR will change during the day but will not change after the daily candle is finished. The daily candle will only finish at 21h00 GMT on FXDD which is still 2 hours to go.

PEACE

LR
